 {\itshape Type\+:} struct

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

Axis state for defining how to react to player input. The settings here control the responsiveness of the axis to player input.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md501}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md501}

\endhead
{\bfseries{Value}}   &Single   &The current value of the axis.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Speed}}   &Single   &The maximum speed of this axis in units/second.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Accel\+Time}}   &Single   &The amount of time in seconds it takes to accelerate to Max\+Speed with the supplied Axis at its maximum value.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Decel\+Time}}   &Single   &The amount of time in seconds it takes to decelerate the axis to zero if the supplied axis is in a neutral position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Input\+Axis\+Name}}   &String   &The name of this axis as specified in \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Input manager. Setting to an empty string will disable the automatic updating of this axis.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Input\+Axis\+Value}}   &Single   &The value of the input axis. A value of 0 means no input. You can drive this directly from a custom input system, or you can set the Axis Name and have the value driven by the internal Input Manager.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Invert\+Input}}   &Boolean   &If checked, then the raw value of the input axis will be inverted before it is used.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Min\+Value}}   &Single   &The minimum value for the axis.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Value}}   &Single   &The maximum value for the axis.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Wrap}}   &Boolean   &If checked, then the axis will wrap around at the min/max values, forming a loop.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md506}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Basic\+Multi\+Channel\+Perlin}{Cinemachine\+Basic\+Multi\+Channel\+Perlin}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md506}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

As a part of the \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Pipeline implementing the Noise stage, this component adds Perlin Noise to the Camera state, in the Correction channel of the Camera\+State.

The noise is created by using a predefined noise profile asset. This defines the shape of the noise over time. You can scale this in amplitude or in time, to produce a large family of different noises using the same profile.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md507}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md507}

\endfirsthead

\endhead
{\bfseries{Is\+Valid}}   &Boolean   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} True if the component is valid, i.\+e. it has a noise definition and is enabled.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Stage}}   &Stage   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} Get the \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Pipeline stage that this component implements. Always returns the Noise stage.~\newline

\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Noise\+Profile}}   &Noise\+Settings   &The asset containing the Noise Profile. Define the frequencies and amplitudes there to make a characteristic noise profile. Make your own or just use one of the many presets.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Amplitude\+Gain}}   &Single   &Gain to apply to the amplitudes defined in the Noise\+Settings asset. 1 is normal. Setting this to 0 completely mutes the noise.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Frequency\+Gain}}   &Single   &Scale factor to apply to the frequencies defined in the Noise\+Settings asset. 1 is normal. Larger magnitudes will make the noise shake more rapidly.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\ttfamily virtual Void Mutate\+Camera\+State(Camera\+State\& cur\+State, Single delta\+Time)}

Applies noise to the Correction channel of the Camera\+State if the delta time is greater than 0. Otherwise, does nothing.

{\itshape Type\+:} struct

Definition of a Camera blend. This struct holds the information necessary to generate a suitable Animation\+Curve for a \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Blend.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md511}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md511}

\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}

\endhead
{\bfseries{Blend\+Curve}}   &Animation\+Curve   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} A normalized Animation\+Curve specifying the interpolation curve for this camera blend. Y-\/axis values must be in range \mbox{[}0,1\mbox{]} (internally clamped within Blender) and time must be in range of \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md512}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md512}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}

\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Style}}   &Style   &Shape of the blend curve.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Cut}}\+: Zero-\/length blend.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Ease\+In\+Out}}\+: S-\/shaped curve, giving a gentle and smooth transition.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Ease\+In}}\+: Linear out of the outgoing shot, and easy into the incoming.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Ease\+Out}}\+: Easy out of the outgoing shot, and linear into the incoming.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Hard\+In}}\+: Easy out of the outgoing, and hard into the incoming.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Hard\+Out}}\+: Hard out of the outgoing, and easy into the incoming.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Linear}}\+: Linear blend. Mechanical-\/looking.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Custom}}\+: Custom blend curve.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Time}}   &Single   &Duration of the blend, in seconds.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Custom\+Curve}}   &Animation\+Curve   &A user-\/defined Animation\+Curve, used only if style is Custom. Curve MUST be normalized, i.\+e. time range \mbox{[}0...1\mbox{]}, value range \mbox{[}0...1\mbox{]}.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\ttfamily Animation\+Curve Get\+Blend\+Curve\+For\+Virtual\+Cameras(\+String from\+Camera\+Name, String to\+Camera\+Name, Animation\+Curve default\+Curve)}

Attempts to find a blend curve which matches the to and from cameras as specified. If no match is found, the function returns either the default blend for this Blender or NULL depending on the state of return\+Default\+On\+No\+Match.

{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

This is a virtual camera "{}manager"{} that owns and manages a collection of child Virtual Cameras. When the camera goes live, these child vcams are enabled, one after another, holding each camera for a designated time. Blends between cameras are specified. The last camera is held indefinitely.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md519}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md519}

{\ttfamily Void Validate\+Instructions()}

Internal API for the inspector editor.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md522}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Brain}{Cinemachine\+Brain}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md522}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Mono\+Behaviour

Cinemachine\+Brain is the link between the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera and the \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Virtual Cameras in the scene. It monitors the priority stack to choose the current Virtual Camera, and blend with another if necessary. Finally and most importantly, it applies the Virtual Camera state to the attached \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera.

The Cinemachine\+Brain is also the place where rules for blending between virtual cameras are defined. Camera blending is an interpolation over time of one virtual camera position and state to another. If you think of virtual cameras as cameramen, then blending is a little like one cameraman smoothly passing the camera to another cameraman. You can specify the time over which to blend, as well as the blend curve shape. Note that a camera cut is just a zero-\/time blend.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md523}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md523}

{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Update\+Method}}   &Update\+Method   &Use Fixed\+Update if all your targets are animated during Fixed\+Update (e.\+g. Smart\+Update is the recommended setting.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Fixed\+Update}}\+: Virtual cameras are updated in sync with the Physics module, in Fixed\+Update.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Late\+Update}}\+: Virtual cameras are updated in Mono\+Behaviour Late\+Update.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Smart\+Update}}\+: Virtual cameras are updated according to how the target is updated.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}

True if the ICinemachine\+Camera the current active camera, or part of a current blend, either directly or indirectly because its parents are live.

{\itshape Returns\+:} True if the camera is live (directly or indirectly) or part of a blend in progress.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md526}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Clear\+Shot}{Cinemachine\+Clear\+Shot}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md526}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

\doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Clear\+Shot is a "{}manager camera"{} that owns and manages a set of Virtual Camera game\+Object children. When Live, the Clear\+Shot will check the children, and choose the one with the best quality shot and make it Live.

This can be a very powerful tool. If the child cameras have Cinemachine\+Collider extensions, they will analyze the scene for target obstructions, optimal target distance, and other items, and report their assessment of shot quality back to the Clear\+Shot parent, who will then choose the best one. You can use this to set up complex multi-\/camera coverage of a scene, and be assured that a clear shot of the target will always be available.

If multiple child cameras have the same shot quality, the one with the highest priority will be chosen.

You can also define custom blends between the Clear\+Shot children.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md527}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md527}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{Description}}   &String   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} Gets a brief debug description of this virtual camera, for use when displaying debug info.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Live\+Child}}   &ICinemachine\+Camera   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get,Set\mbox{]}} Get the current "{}best"{} child virtual camera, that would be chosen if the Clear\+Shot camera were active.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{State}}   &Camera\+State   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} The Camera\+State of the currently live child.    \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md530}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Collider}{Cinemachine\+Collider}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md530}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Extension

An add-\/on module for \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Virtual Camera that post-\/processes the final position of the virtual camera. Based on the supplied settings, the Collider will attempt to preserve the line of sight with the Look\+At target of the virtual camera by moving away from objects that will obstruct the view.

Additionally, the Collider can be used to assess the shot quality and report this as a field in the camera State.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md531}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md531}

{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Camera\+Radius}}   &Single   &Camera will try to maintain this distance from any obstacle. Try to keep this value small. Increase it if you are seeing inside obstacles due to a large FOV on the camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Strategy}}   &Resolution\+Strategy   &The way in which the Collider will attempt to preserve sight of the target.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Pull\+Camera\+Forward}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Preserve\+Camera\+Height}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Preserve\+Camera\+Distance}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+Effort}}   &Int32   &Upper limit on how many obstacle hits to process. Higher numbers may impact performance. In most environments, 4 is enough.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Damping}}   &Single   &The gradualness of collision resolution. Higher numbers will move the camera more gradually away from obstructions.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Optimal\+Target\+Distance}}   &Single   &If greater than zero, a higher score will be given to shots when the target is closer to this distance. Set this to zero to disable this feature.   \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md534}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Composer}{Cinemachine\+Composer}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md534}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

This is a Cinemachine\+Component in the Aim section of the component pipeline. Its job is to aim the camera at the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Look\+At target object, with configurable offsets, damping, and composition rules.

The composer does not change the camera\textquotesingle{}s position. It will only pan and tilt the camera where it is, in order to get the desired framing. To move the camera, you have to use the virtual camera\textquotesingle{}s Body section.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md535}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md535}
\tabulinesep=1mm

\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot

\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{Is\+Valid}}   &Boolean   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} True if component is enabled and has a Look\+At defined.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Stage}}   &Stage   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} Get the \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Pipeline stage that this component implements. Always returns the Aim stage.~\newline

    \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md536}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md536}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{On\+GUICallback}}   &Action   &Used by the Inspector Editor to display on-\/screen guides.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Tracked\+Object\+Offset}}   &Vector3   &Target offset from the target object\textquotesingle{}s center in target-\/local space. Use this to fine-\/tune the tracking target position when the desired area is not the tracked object\textquotesingle{}s center.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Time}}   &Single   &This setting will instruct the composer to adjust its target offset based on the motion of the target. The composer will look at a point where it estimates the target will be this many seconds into the future. Note that this setting is sensitive to noisy animation, and can amplify the noise, resulting in undesirable camera jitter. If the camera jitters unacceptably when the target is in motion, turn down this setting, or animate the target more smoothly.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Smoothing}}   &Single   &Controls the smoothness of the lookahead algorithm. Larger values smooth out jittery predictions and also increase prediction lag.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+IgnoreY}}   &Boolean   &If checked, movement along the Y axis will be ignored for lookahead calculations.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Horizontal\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to follow the target in the screen-\/horizontal direction. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly orienting the camera to keep the target in the dead zone. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different vertical and horizontal settings can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Vertical\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to follow the target in the screen-\/vertical direction. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly orienting the camera to keep the target in the dead zone. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different vertical and horizontal settings can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenX}}   &Single   &Horizontal screen position for target. The camera will rotate to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenY}}   &Single   &Vertical screen position for target, The camera will rotate to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &Camera will not rotate horizontally if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &Camera will not rotate vertically if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually rotate horizontally to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually rotate vertically to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasX}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position horizontally away from the center of the soft zone.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasY}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position vertically away from the center of the soft zone.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md537}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Methods}{Methods}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md537}

\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Width}}   &Single   &The shot width to maintain, in world units, at target distance.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Damping}}   &Single   &Increase this value to soften the aggressiveness of the follow-\/zoom. Small numbers are more responsive, larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Min\+FOV}}   &Single   &Lower limit for the FOV that this behaviour will generate.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+FOV}}   &Single   &Upper limit for the FOV that this behaviour will generate.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\ttfamily protected virtual Void Post\+Pipeline\+Stage\+Callback(Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base vcam, Stage stage, Camera\+State\& state, Single delta\+Time)}

Callback to preform the zoom adjustment.

\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md551}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Framing\+Transposer}{Cinemachine\+Framing\+Transposer}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md551}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

This is a \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Component in the Body section of the component pipeline. Its job is to position the camera in a fixed screen-\/space relationship to the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Follow target object, with offsets and damping.

The camera will be first moved along the camera Z axis until the Follow target is at the desired distance from the camera\textquotesingle{}s X-\/Y plane. The camera will then be moved in its XY plane until the Follow target is at the desired point on the camera\textquotesingle{}s screen.

The Framing\+Tansposer will only change the camera\textquotesingle{}s position in space. It will not re-\/orient or otherwise aim the camera.

For this component to work properly, the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Look\+At target must be null. The Follow target will define what the camera is looking at.

If the Follow target is a Cinemachine\+Target\+Group, then additional controls will be available to dynamically adjust the camera\textquotesingle{}s view in order to frame the entire group.

Although this component was designed for orthographic cameras, it works equally well with perspective cameras and can be used in 3D environments.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md552}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md552}

{\bfseries{On\+GUICallback}}   &Action   &Used by the Inspector Editor to display on-\/screen guides.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Time}}   &Single   &This setting will instruct the composer to adjust its target offset based on the motion of the target. The composer will look at a point where it estimates the target will be this many seconds into the future. Note that this setting is sensitive to noisy animation, and can amplify the noise, resulting in undesirable camera jitter. If the camera jitters unacceptably when the target is in motion, turn down this setting, or animate the target more smoothly.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Smoothing}}   &Single   &Controls the smoothness of the lookahead algorithm. Larger values smooth out jittery predictions and also increase prediction lag.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+IgnoreY}}   &Boolean   &If checked, movement along the Y axis will be ignored for lookahead calculations.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+XDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the X-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s x-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Y-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s y-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ZDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Z-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s z-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenX}}   &Single   &Horizontal screen position for target. The camera will move to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenY}}   &Single   &Vertical screen position for target, The camera will move to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Camera\+Distance}}   &Single   &The distance along the camera axis that will be maintained from the Follow target.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &Camera will not move horizontally if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &Camera will not move vertically if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Depth}}   &Single   &The camera will not move along its z-\/axis if the Follow target is within this distance of the specified camera distance.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Unlimited\+Soft\+Zone}}   &Boolean   &If checked, then soft zone will be unlimited in size.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually move horizontally to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually move vertically to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasX}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position horizontally away from the center of the soft zone.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasY}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position vertically away from the center of the soft zone.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Group\+Framing\+Mode}}   &Framing\+Mode   &What screen dimensions to consider when framing. Can be Horizontal, Vertical, or both.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Horizontal}}\+: Consider only the horizontal dimension. Vertical framing is ignored.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Vertical}}\+: Consider only the vertical dimension. Horizontal framing is ignored.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Horizontal\+And\+Vertical}}\+: The larger of the horizontal and vertical dimensions will dominate, to get the best fit.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{None}}\+: Don\textquotesingle{}t do any framing adjustment.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Adjustment\+Mode}}   &Adjustment\+Mode   &How to adjust the camera to get the desired framing. You can zoom, dolly in/out, or do both.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Zoom\+Only}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Dolly\+Only}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Dolly\+Then\+Zoom}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Group\+Framing\+Size}}   &Single   &The bounding box of the targets should occupy this amount of the screen space. 1 means fill the whole screen. 0.\+5 means fill half the screen, etc.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Dolly\+In}}   &Single   &The maximum distance toward the target that this behaviour is allowed to move the camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Dolly\+Out}}   &Single   &The maximum distance away the target that this behaviour is allowed to move the camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+Distance}}   &Single   &Set this to limit how close to the target the camera can get.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+Distance}}   &Single   &Set this to limit how far from the target the camera can get.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+FOV}}   &Single   &If adjusting FOV, will not set the FOV lower than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+FOV}}   &Single   &If adjusting FOV, will not set the FOV higher than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+Ortho\+Size}}   &Single   &If adjusting Orthographic Size, will not set it lower than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+Ortho\+Size}}   &Single   &If adjusting Orthographic Size, will not set it higher than this.   \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md555}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Free\+Look}{Cinemachine\+Free\+Look}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md555}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

A \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Camera geared towards a 3rd person camera experience. The camera orbits around its subject with three separate camera rigs defining rings around the target. Each rig has its own radius, height offset, composer, and lens settings. Depending on the camera\textquotesingle{}s position along the spline connecting these three rigs, these settings are interpolated to give the final camera position and state.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md556}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md556}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}

\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead

{\bfseries{State}}   &Camera\+State   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} The camera state, which will be a blend of the child rig states.    \\\cline{1-3}

{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline

-\/ {\bfseries{Spherical}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Cylindrical}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Common\+Lens}}   &Boolean   &If enabled, this lens setting will apply to all three child rigs, otherwise the child rig lens settings will be used.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lens}}   &Lens\+Settings   &Specifies the lens properties of this Virtual Camera. This generally mirrors the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera\textquotesingle{}s lens settings, and will be used to drive the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} camera when the vcam is active.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YAxis}}   &Axis\+State   &The Vertical axis. Value is 0..1. Chooses how to blend the child rigs.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YAxis\+Recentering}}   &Recentering   &Controls how automatic recentering of the Y axis is accomplished.    \\\cline{1-3}

{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Heading}}   &Heading   &The definition of Forward. Camera will follow behind.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Recenter\+To\+Target\+Heading}}   &Recentering   &Controls how automatic recentering of the X axis is accomplished.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Binding\+Mode}}   &Binding\+Mode   &The coordinate space to use when interpreting the offset from the target. This is also used to set the camera\textquotesingle{}s Up vector, which will be maintained when aiming the camera.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+On\+Assign}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame at the moment when the virtual camera was enabled, or when the target was assigned.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the tilt and roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+No\+Roll}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{World\+Space}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a world space offset.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Simple\+Follow\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Offsets will be calculated relative to the target, using Camera-\/local axes.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Spline\+Curvature}}   &Single   &Controls how taut is the line that connects the rigs\textquotesingle{} orbits, which determines final placement on the Y axis.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Orbits}}   &Orbit\mbox{[}\mbox{]}   &The radius and height of the three orbiting rigs.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Cinemachine\+GUIDebugger\+Callback}}   &Action   &This is deprecated. It is here to support the soon-\/to-\/be-\/removed \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Debugger in the Editor.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Excluded\+Properties\+In\+Inspector}}   &String\mbox{[}\mbox{]}   &Inspector control -\/ Use for hiding sections of the Inspector UI.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lock\+Stage\+In\+Inspector}}   &Stage\mbox{[}\mbox{]}   &Inspector control -\/ Use for enabling sections of the Inspector UI.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Priority}}   &Int32   &The priority will determine which camera becomes active based on the state of other cameras and this camera. Higher numbers have greater priority.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md558}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Methods}{Methods}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md558}
{\ttfamily protected virtual Void On\+Validate()}

Enforce bounds for fields, when changed in inspector.

{\ttfamily Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera Get\+Rig(\+Int32 i)}

Get a child rig.

{\itshape Returns\+:} The local offset (back + up) of the camera WRT its target based on the supplied t-\/value.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md559}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Group\+Composer}{Cinemachine\+Group\+Composer}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md559}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Composer

This is a Cinemachine\+Component in the Aim section of the component pipeline. Its job is to aim the camera at a target object, with configurable offsets, damping, and composition rules.

In addition, if the target is a Cinemachine\+Target\+Group, the behaviour will adjust the FOV and the camera distance to ensure that the entire group of targets is framed properly.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md560}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md560}

\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}

\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Group\+Framing\+Size}}   &Single   &The bounding box of the targets should occupy this amount of the screen space. 1 means fill the whole screen. 0.\+5 means fill half the screen, etc.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Framing\+Mode}}   &Framing\+Mode   &What screen dimensions to consider when framing. Can be Horizontal, Vertical, or both.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Horizontal}}\+: Consider only the horizontal dimension. Vertical framing is ignored.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Vertical}}\+: Consider only the vertical dimension. Horizontal framing is ignored.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Horizontal\+And\+Vertical}}\+: The larger of the horizontal and vertical dimensions will dominate, to get the best fit.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Frame\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to frame the group. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly adjusting the camera to keep the group in the frame. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Adjustment\+Mode}}   &Adjustment\+Mode   &How to adjust the camera to get the desired framing. You can zoom, dolly in/out, or do both.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Zoom\+Only}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Dolly\+Only}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Dolly\+Then\+Zoom}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Dolly\+In}}   &Single   &The maximum distance toward the target that this behaviour is allowed to move the camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Max\+Dolly\+Out}}   &Single   &The maximum distance away the target that this behaviour is allowed to move the camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+Distance}}   &Single   &Set this to limit how close to the target the camera can get.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+Distance}}   &Single   &Set this to limit how far from the target the camera can get.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+FOV}}   &Single   &If adjusting FOV, will not set the FOV lower than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+FOV}}   &Single   &If adjusting FOV, will not set the FOV higher than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Minimum\+Ortho\+Size}}   &Single   &If adjusting Orthographic Size, will not set it lower than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Maximum\+Ortho\+Size}}   &Single   &If adjusting Orthographic Size, will not set it higher than this.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{On\+GUICallback}}   &Action   &Used by the Inspector Editor to display on-\/screen guides.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Tracked\+Object\+Offset}}   &Vector3   &Target offset from the target object\textquotesingle{}s center in target-\/local space. Use this to fine-\/tune the tracking target position when the desired area is not the tracked object\textquotesingle{}s center.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Time}}   &Single   &This setting will instruct the composer to adjust its target offset based on the motion of the target. The composer will look at a point where it estimates the target will be this many seconds into the future. Note that this setting is sensitive to noisy animation, and can amplify the noise, resulting in undesirable camera jitter. If the camera jitters unacceptably when the target is in motion, turn down this setting, or animate the target more smoothly.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+Smoothing}}   &Single   &Controls the smoothness of the lookahead algorithm. Larger values smooth out jittery predictions and also increase prediction lag.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Lookahead\+IgnoreY}}   &Boolean   &If checked, movement along the Y axis will be ignored for lookahead calculations.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Horizontal\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to follow the target in the screen-\/horizontal direction. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly orienting the camera to keep the target in the dead zone. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different vertical and horizontal settings can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Vertical\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to follow the target in the screen-\/vertical direction. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly orienting the camera to keep the target in the dead zone. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different vertical and horizontal settings can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenX}}   &Single   &Horizontal screen position for target. The camera will rotate to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ScreenY}}   &Single   &Vertical screen position for target, The camera will rotate to position the tracked object here.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &Camera will not rotate horizontally if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Dead\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &Camera will not rotate vertically if the target is within this range of the position.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Width}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually rotate horizontally to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Soft\+Zone\+Height}}   &Single   &When target is within this region, camera will gradually rotate vertically to re-\/align towards the desired position, depending on the damping speed.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasX}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position horizontally away from the center of the soft zone.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+BiasY}}   &Single   &A non-\/zero bias will move the target position vertically away from the center of the soft zone.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md569}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Mixing\+Camera}{Cinemachine\+Mixing\+Camera}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md569}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

Cinemachine\+Mixing\+Camera is a "{}manager camera"{} that takes on the state of the weighted average of the states of its child virtual cameras.

A fixed number of slots are made available for cameras, rather than a dynamic array. We do it this way in order to support weight animation from the \doxylink{namespace_timeline}{Timeline}. \doxylink{namespace_timeline}{Timeline} cannot animate array elements.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md570}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md570}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md573}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Orbital\+Transposer}{Cinemachine\+Orbital\+Transposer}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md573}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Transposer

This is a Cinemachine\+Component in the Body section of the component pipeline. Its job is to position the camera in a variable relationship to a the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Follow target object, with offsets and damping.

This component is typically used to implement a camera that follows its target. It can accept player input from an input device, which allows the player to dynamically control the relationship between the camera and the target, for example with a joystick.

The Orbital\+Transposer introduces the concept of {\bfseries{Heading}}, which is the direction in which the target is moving, and the Orbital\+Transposer will attempt to position the camera in relationship to the heading, which is by default directly behind the target. You can control the default relationship by adjusting the Heading Bias setting.

If you attach an input controller to the Orbital\+Transposer, then the player can also control the way the camera positions itself in relation to the target heading. This allows the camera to move to any spot on an orbit around the target.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md574}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md574}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Heading}}   &Heading   &The definition of Forward. Camera will follow behind.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Recenter\+To\+Target\+Heading}}   &Recentering   &Automatic heading recentering. The settings here defines how the camera will reposition itself in the absence of player input.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+XAxis}}   &Axis\+State   &Heading Control. The settings here control the behaviour of the camera in response to the player\textquotesingle{}s input.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Heading\+Is\+Slave}}   &Boolean   &Drive the x-\/axis setting programmatically. Automatic heading updating will be disabled.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Binding\+Mode}}   &Binding\+Mode   &The coordinate space to use when interpreting the offset from the target. This is also used to set the camera\textquotesingle{}s Up vector, which will be maintained when aiming the camera.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+On\+Assign}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame at the moment when the virtual camera was enabled, or when the target was assigned.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the tilt and roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+No\+Roll}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{World\+Space}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a world space offset.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Simple\+Follow\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Offsets will be calculated relative to the target, using Camera-\/local axes.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Follow\+Offset}}   &Vector3   &The distance vector that the transposer will attempt to maintain from the Follow target.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+XDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the X-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s x-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Y-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s y-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ZDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Z-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s z-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Pitch\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s X angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Yaw\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Y angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Roll\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Z angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\bfseries{delta\+Time}}   &Single   &Used for damping. If less than 0, no damping is done.   \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md576}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Orbital\+Transposer.\+Heading}{Cinemachine\+Orbital\+Transposer.\+Heading}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md576}
{\itshape Type\+:} struct

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

How the "{}forward"{} direction is defined. Orbital offset is in relation to the forward direction.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md577}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md577}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Definition}}   &Heading\+Definition   &How \textquotesingle{}forward\textquotesingle{} is defined. The camera will be placed by default behind the target. Position\+Delta will consider \textquotesingle{}forward\textquotesingle{} to be the direction in which the target is moving.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Position\+Delta}}\+: Target heading calculated from the difference between its position on the last update and current frame.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Velocity}}\+: Target heading calculated from its Rigidbody\textquotesingle{}s velocity. If no Rigidbody exists, it will fall back to Heading\+Derivation\+Mode.\+Position\+Delta.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Target\+Forward}}\+: Target heading calculated from the Target Transform\textquotesingle{}s euler Y angle.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{World\+Forward}}\+: Default heading is a constant world space heading.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Velocity\+Filter\+Strength}}   &Int32   &Size of the velocity sampling window for target heading filter. This filters out irregularities in the target\textquotesingle{}s movement. Used only if deriving heading from target\textquotesingle{}s movement (Position\+Delta or Velocity).    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Bias}}   &Single   &Where the camera is placed when the X-\/axis value is zero. This is a rotation in degrees around the Y axis. When this value is 0, the camera will be placed behind the target. Nonzero offsets will rotate the zero position around the target.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Path\+Base

Defines a world-\/space path, consisting of an array of waypoints, each of which has position, tangent, and roll settings. Bezier interpolation is performed between the waypoints, to get a smooth and continuous path.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md579}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md579}

{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

This is a Cinemachine\+Component in the Aim section of the component pipeline. Its job is to aim the camera in response to the user\textquotesingle{}s mouse or joystick input.

The composer does not change the camera\textquotesingle{}s position. It will only pan and tilt the camera where it is, in order to get the desired framing. To move the camera, you have to use the virtual camera\textquotesingle{}s Body section.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md587}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md587}

{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Path\+Base

Defines a world-\/space path, consisting of an array of waypoints, each of which has position and roll settings. Bezier interpolation is performed between the waypoints, to get a smooth and continuous path. The path will pass through all waypoints, and (unlike Cinemachine\+Path) first and second order continuity is guaranteed.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md594}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md594}

\endfirsthead

\endhead

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md599}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+State\+Driven\+Camera}{Cinemachine\+State\+Driven\+Camera}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md599}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

This is a virtual camera "{}manager"{} that owns and manages a collection of child Virtual Cameras. These child vcams are mapped to individual states in an animation state machine, allowing you to associate specific vcams to specific animation states. When that state is active in the state machine, then the associated camera will be activated.

You can define custom blends and transitions between child cameras.

In order to use this behaviour, you must have an animated target (i.\+e. an object animated with a state machine) to drive the behaviour.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md600}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md600}

{\ttfamily virtual Void Internal\+Update\+Camera\+State(\+Vector3 world\+Up, Single delta\+Time)}

Internal use only. Do not call this method. Called by Cinemachine\+Core at designated update time so the vcam can position itself and track its targets. This implementation updates all the children, chooses the best one, and implements any required blending.

{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Mono\+Behaviour

Defines a group of target objects, each with a radius and a weight. The weight is used when calculating the average position of the target group. Higher-\/weighted members of the group will count more. The bounding box is calculated by taking the member positions, weight, and radii into account.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md607}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md607}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{Bounding\+Box}}   &Bounds   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} The axis-\/aligned bounding box of the group, computed using the targets positions and radii.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Is\+Empty}}   &Boolean   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} Return true if there are no members with weight \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md608}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md608}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot

\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Position\+Mode}}   &Position\+Mode   &How the group\textquotesingle{}s position is calculated. Select Group\+Center for the center of the bounding box, and Group\+Average for a weighted average of the positions of the members.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Group\+Center}}\+: Group position will be the center of the group\textquotesingle{}s axis-\/aligned bounding box.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Group\+Average}}\+: Group position will be the weighted average of the positions of the members.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Rotation\+Mode}}   &Rotation\+Mode   &How the group\textquotesingle{}s rotation is calculated. Select Manual to use the value in the group\textquotesingle{}s transform, and Group\+Average for a weighted average of the orientations of the members.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Manual}}\+: Manually set in the group\textquotesingle{}s transform.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Group\+Average}}\+: Weighted average of the orientation of its members.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Update\+Method}}   &Update\+Method   &When to update the group\textquotesingle{}s transform based on the position of the group members.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Update}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Fixed\+Update}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Late\+Update}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Targets}}   &Target\mbox{[}\mbox{]}   &The target objects, together with their weights and radii, that will contribute to the group\textquotesingle{}s average position, orientation, and size.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md609}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Methods}{Methods}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md609}

{\itshape Type\+:} struct

Holds the information that represents a member of the group.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md611}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md611}

\endhead
{\bfseries{target}}   &Transform   &The target objects. This object\textquotesingle{}s position and orientation will contribute to the group\textquotesingle{}s average position and orientation, in accordance with its weight.    \\\cline{1-3}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md612}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Tracked\+Dolly}{Cinemachine\+Tracked\+Dolly}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md612}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

A \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Virtual Camera Body component that constrains camera motion to a Cinemachine\+Path. The camera can move along the path.

This behaviour can operate in two modes\+: manual positioning, and Auto-\/\+Dolly positioning. In Manual mode, the camera\textquotesingle{}s position is specified by animating the Path Position field. In Auto-\/\+Dolly mode, the Path Position field is animated automatically every frame by finding the position on the path that\textquotesingle{}s closest to the virtual camera\textquotesingle{}s Follow target.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md613}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md613}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{Is\+Valid}}   &Boolean   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} True if component is enabled and has a path.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Stage}}   &Stage   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} Get the \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Pipeline stage that this component implements. Always returns the Body stage.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Body}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Aim}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Noise}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Finalize}}~\newline
   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md614}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md614}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Path}}   &Cinemachine\+Path\+Base   &The path to which the camera will be constrained. This must be non-\/null.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Path\+Position}}   &Single   &The position along the path at which the camera will be placed. This can be animated directly, or set automatically by the Auto-\/\+Dolly feature to get as close as possible to the Follow target. The value is interpreted according to the Position Units setting.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Position\+Units}}   &Position\+Units   &How to interpret Path Position. If set to Path Units, values are as follows\+: 0 represents the first waypoint on the path, 1 is the second, and so on. Values in-\/between are points on the path in between the waypoints. If set to Distance, then Path Position represents distance along the path.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Path\+Units}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Distance}}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Normalized}}~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Path\+Offset}}   &Vector3   &Where to put the camera relative to the path position. X is perpendicular to the path, Y is up, and Z is parallel to the path. This allows the camera to be offset from the path itself (as if on a tripod, for example).    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+XDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain its position in a direction perpendicular to the path. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s x-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain its position in the path-\/local up direction. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s y-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ZDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain its position in a direction parallel to the path. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s z-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Camera\+Up}}   &Camera\+Up\+Mode   &How to set the virtual camera\textquotesingle{}s Up vector. This will affect the screen composition, because the camera Aim behaviours will always try to respect the Up direction.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Default}}\+: Leave the camera\textquotesingle{}s up vector alone. It will be set according to the Brain\textquotesingle{}s World\+Up.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Path}}\+: Take the up vector from the path\textquotesingle{}s up vector at the current point.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Path\+No\+Roll}}\+: Take the up vector from the path\textquotesingle{}s up vector at the current point, but with the roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Follow\+Target}}\+: Take the up vector from the Follow target\textquotesingle{}s up vector.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Follow\+Target\+No\+Roll}}\+: Take the up vector from the Follow target\textquotesingle{}s up vector, but with the roll zeroed out.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Pitch\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s X angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Yaw\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Y angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Roll\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Z angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Auto\+Dolly}}   &Auto\+Dolly   &Controls how automatic dollying occurs. A Follow target is necessary to use this feature.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

{\ttfamily virtual Void Mutate\+Camera\+State(Camera\+State\& cur\+State, Single delta\+Time)}

Positions the virtual camera according to the transposer rules.

\tabulinesep=1mm

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md616}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Tracked\+Dolly.\+Auto\+Dolly}{Cinemachine\+Tracked\+Dolly.\+Auto\+Dolly}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md616}
{\itshape Type\+:} struct

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

Controls how automatic dollying occurs.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md617}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md617}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot
\hline
\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Enabled}}   &Boolean   &If checked, will enable automatic dolly, which chooses a path position that is as close as possible to the Follow target. Note\+: this can have significant performance impact.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Position\+Offset}}   &Single   &Offset, in current position units, from the closest point on the path to the follow target.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Search\+Radius}}   &Int32   &Search up to how many waypoints on either side of the current position. Use 0 for Entire path.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Search\+Resolution}}   &Int32   &We search between waypoints by dividing the segment into this many straight pieces. The higher the number, the more accurate the result, but performance is proportionally slower for higher numbers.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md618}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Transposer}{Cinemachine\+Transposer}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md618}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Component\+Base

This is a Cinemachine\+Component in the Body section of the component pipeline. Its job is to position the camera in a fixed relationship to the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Follow target object, with offsets and damping.

The Transposer will only change the camera\textquotesingle{}s position in space. It will not re-\/orient or otherwise aim the camera. To that, you need to instruct the vcam in the Aim section of its pipeline.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md619}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md619}
