\endhead
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Binding\+Mode}}   &Binding\+Mode   &The coordinate space to use when interpreting the offset from the target. This is also used to set the camera\textquotesingle{}s Up vector, which will be maintained when aiming the camera.~\newline
{\itshape Possible Values\+:}~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+On\+Assign}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame at the moment when the virtual camera was enabled, or when the target was assigned.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the tilt and roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target\+No\+Roll}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a frame of reference consisting of the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame, with the roll zeroed out.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Lock\+To\+Target}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using the target\textquotesingle{}s local frame.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{World\+Space}}\+: Camera will be bound to the Follow target using a world space offset.~\newline
-\/ {\bfseries{Simple\+Follow\+With\+World\+Up}}\+: Offsets will be calculated relative to the target, using Camera-\/local axes.~\newline
    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Follow\+Offset}}   &Vector3   &The distance vector that the transposer will attempt to maintain from the Follow target.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+XDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the X-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s x-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+YDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Y-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s y-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+ZDamping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to maintain the offset in the Z-\/axis. Small numbers are more responsive, rapidly translating the camera to keep the target\textquotesingle{}s z-\/axis offset. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera. Using different settings per axis can yield a wide range of camera behaviors.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Pitch\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s X angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Yaw\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Y angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Roll\+Damping}}   &Single   &How aggressively the camera tries to track the target rotation\textquotesingle{}s Z angle. Small numbers are more responsive. Larger numbers give a more heavy slowly responding camera.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md622}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera}{Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md622}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Cinemachine\+Virtual\+Camera\+Base

{\itshape Implements\+:} ICinemachine\+Camera

This behaviour is intended to be attached to an empty Transform Game\+Object, and it represents a Virtual Camera within the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} scene.

The Virtual Camera will animate its Transform according to the rules contained in its Cinemachine\+Component pipeline (Aim, Body, and Noise). When the virtual camera is Live, the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} camera will assume the position and orientation of the virtual camera.

A virtual camera is not a camera. Instead, it can be thought of as a camera controller, not unlike a cameraman. It can drive the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera and control its position, orientation, lens settings, and Post\+Processing effects. Each Virtual Camera owns its own \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine} Component Pipeline, through which you provide the instructions for dynamically tracking specific game objects.

A virtual camera is very lightweight, and does no rendering of its own. It merely tracks interesting Game\+Objects, and positions itself accordingly. A typical game can have dozens of virtual cameras, each set up to follow a particular character or capture a particular event.

A Virtual Camera can be in any of three states\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{Live}}\+: The virtual camera is actively controlling the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera. The virtual camera is tracking its targets and being updated every frame.
\item {\bfseries{Standby}}\+: The virtual camera is tracking its targets and being updated every frame, but no \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera is actively being controlled by it. This is the state of a virtual camera that is enabled in the scene but perhaps at a lower priority than the Live virtual camera.
\item {\bfseries{Disabled}}\+: The virtual camera is present but disabled in the scene. It is not actively tracking its targets and so consumes no processing power. However, the virtual camera can be made live from the \doxylink{namespace_timeline}{Timeline}.
\end{DoxyItemize}

The \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera can be driven by any virtual camera in the scene. The game logic can choose the virtual camera to make live by manipulating the virtual cameras\textquotesingle{} enabled flags and their priorities, based on game logic.

In order to be driven by a virtual camera, the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera must have a Cinemachine\+Brain behaviour, which will select the most eligible virtual camera based on its priority or on other criteria, and will manage blending.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md623}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md623}
\tabulinesep=1mm
\begin{longtabu}spread 0pt [c]{*{3}{|X[-1]}|}

\endfirsthead

\endhead
{\bfseries{State}}   &Camera\+State   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get\mbox{]}} The Camera\+State object holds all of the information necessary to position the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} camera. It is the output of this class.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Look\+At}}   &Transform   &{\itshape \mbox{[}Get,Set\mbox{]}} Get the Look\+At target for the Aim component in the Cinemachine\+Pipeline. {\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Look\+At}}   &Transform   &The object that the camera wants to look at (the Aim target). If this is null, then the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Transform orientation will define the camera\textquotesingle{}s orientation.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Follow}}   &Transform   &The object that the camera wants to move with (the Body target). If this is null, then the vcam\textquotesingle{}s Transform position will define the camera\textquotesingle{}s position.    \\\cline{1-3}

{\bfseries{m\+\_\+\+Priority}}   &Int32   &The priority will determine which camera becomes active based on the state of other cameras and this camera. Higher numbers have greater priority.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}
\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md625}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Methods}{Methods}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md625}
{\ttfamily virtual Void Internal\+Update\+Camera\+State(\+Vector3 world\+Up, Single delta\+Time)}

Internal use only. Do not call this method. Called by Cinemachine\+Core at the appropriate Update time so the vcam can position itself and track its targets. This class will invoke its pipeline and generate a Camera\+State for this frame.

{\itshape Type\+:} struct

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

Describes the FOV and clip planes for a camera. This generally mirrors the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} Camera\textquotesingle{}s lens settings, and will be used to drive the \doxylink{namespace_unity}{Unity} camera when the vcam is active.\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md627}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fields}{Fields}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md627}

\endhead
{\bfseries{Field\+Of\+View}}   &Single   &This is the camera view in vertical degrees. For cinematic people, a 50mm lens on a super-\/35mm sensor would equal a 19.\+6 degree FOV.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Orthographic\+Size}}   &Single   &When using an orthographic camera, this defines the half-\/height, in world coordinates, of the camera view.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Near\+Clip\+Plane}}   &Single   &This defines the near region in the renderable range of the camera frustum. Raising this value will stop the game from drawing things near the camera, which can sometimes come in handy. Larger values will also increase your shadow resolution.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Far\+Clip\+Plane}}   &Single   &This defines the far region of the renderable range of the camera frustum. Typically you want to set this value as low as possible without cutting off desired distant objects.    \\\cline{1-3}
{\bfseries{Dutch}}   &Single   &Camera Z roll, or tilt, in degrees.   \\\cline{1-3}
\end{longtabu}

Make sure lens settings are sane. Call this from On\+Validate().\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md629}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Noise\+Settings}{Noise\+Settings}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md629}
{\itshape Type\+:} class

{\itshape Namespace\+:} \doxylink{namespace_cinemachine}{Cinemachine}

{\itshape Inherits\+:} Scriptable\+Object

This is an asset that defines a noise profile. A noise profile is the shape of the noise as a function of time. You can build arbitrarily complex shapes by combining different base perlin noise frequencies at different amplitudes.

The frequencies and amplitudes should be chosen with care, to ensure an interesting noise quality that is not obviously repetitive.

As a mathematical side-\/note, any arbitrary periodic curve can be broken down into a series of fixed-\/amplitude sine-\/waves added together. This is called fourier decomposition, and is the basis of much signal processing. It doesn\textquotesingle{}t really have much to do with this asset, but it\textquotesingle{}s super interesting!\hypertarget{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md630}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Properties}{Properties}}\label{md__hey_tea_9_2_library_2_package_cache_2com_8unity_8cinemachine_0d2_89_87_2_documentation_0i_2cinemachine_a_p_i_autotoc_md630}
\tabulinesep=1mm

\endfirsthead
\hline
\endfoot

\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Name}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Type}   }&\PBS\centering \cellcolor{\tableheadbgcolor}\textbf{ {\itshape Description}    }\\\cline{1-3}
\endhead
